class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>MODULE 4: COMMUNITY FIRST AID</p>
<p>Code: FIA 104
Hours: 40
Credit: 4</p>
<p>11.1 Module competence
This module is designed to enable the learner provide first aid services at community level.</p>
<p>11.2 Module Outcomes
By the end of this module, the learner should;</p>
<ol>
<li>Apply concepts and principles in first aid</li>
<li>Perform Cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) to an unresponsive adult, child and infant</li>
<li>Manage casualties Apply first aid skills in relieving choking, drowning victim</li>
<li>Identify and use the contents in First aid kit</li>
<li>Manage persons with major illness</li>
<li>Apply first aid principles in moving and handling casualties</li>
</ol>
<p>11.3 Module Units</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Unit Name</th><th>Hours Theory</th><th>Practical</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1. Introduction to Community first aid</td><td>05</td><td>00</td></tr><tr><td>2. Cardiopulmonary Resuscitation (CPR)</td><td>02</td><td>04</td></tr><tr><td>3. Managing emergency situations</td><td>04</td><td>04</td></tr><tr><td>4. First Aid Kit</td><td>02</td><td>03</td></tr><tr><td>5. Major illnesses</td><td>06</td><td>04</td></tr><tr><td>6. Moving and handling Casualties</td><td>02</td><td>04</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>11.3 Module Content</p>
<p>Community First Aid; Introduction, definitions of terms: First aid: First Aider: Emergency First Aid, Cardiopulmonary resustation Triage, Historical back ground of First Aid, Symbols used in first Aid, Scope of first Aid, objectives of first aid, responsibilities of a first aider, eight qualities of a first aider, basic principles and rules of first Aid. Casualty assessment Primary survey, Recovery position Secondary assessment. Infection prevention Incident management: AMEGA principles (assessing the area, managing the incident, emergency aid, get help, deal with aftermath), prioritizing the incident, chain of survival road traffic accidents Cardiopulmonary Resuscitation; Scene assessment, checking for responsiveness, activating the EMS, CPR (hands only) one and two rescuers. Choking; infant, adult, drowning First Aid Checklist; Content and supplies checklist. Management of various emergency conditions - Medical emergencies conditions: hypoglycemia, hyperglycemia, allergy, fever, meningitis, headache, ear ache and tooth ache, abdomen pain, vomiting and diarrhea, bites and stings, foreign bodies, Emergency child birth: Stages of labor, signs and symptoms of labor stroke, heart attack, acute asthma attack, convulsions, poisoning, bleeding, burns. Management of body injuries: fractures, dislocations, wounds, sprains, strains, head injuries, crush injuries, burns and scalds, extremes of temperatures, eye injuries, Moving and handling; positioning an ill or injured person, transfer of an injured patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="teaching-and-learning-resources">Teaching and Learning Resources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#teaching-and-learning-resources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction-to-first-aid">INTRODUCTION TO FIRST AID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-first-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="terms-definitions">Terms definitions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#terms-definitions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>First Aid: is the immediate and temporary care given to an injured or sick person until the services of a qualified doctor are obtained with such material as may be available. The first aid is not an end by itself. It indicates that the person is in need of a secondary aid</p>
<p>Medical Aid: refers to treatment by a doctor either on the sport at home or in the hospital</p>
<p><strong>Emergency first Aid</strong>—the first response to a life-threatening (or limb-threatening) medical emergency, either an illness or an injury. It's often called <em>first responder aid</em>. More advanced medical care will happen after first aid in this case. This type of first aid includes; CPR, clearing an airway obstruction, responding to <em>anaphylactic shock</em>, splinting a <em>broken bone</em>, and severe <em>bleeding control</em>.</p>
<p><strong>Cardiopulmonary resuscitation</strong>: procedure to restore breathing and circulation</p>
<p><strong>The Primary Survey</strong> - a quick way for you to find out if someone has any injuries or conditions which are life-threatening. The five elements of primary survey include checking for, danger, Response, Airway, breathing, and circulation</p>
<p>Triage: A process of determining the priority of patients treatment by severity of their condition or likelihood of recovery</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-aider">First aider:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-aider" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The person who renders emergency service on the spot until the medical aid is obtained.</p>
<p>A sound knowledge based on first aid enables a fist aider to give skilled services during accidents and sudden illness to preserve life promote recovery and prevent injury or illness being aggravated until the medical aid has been obtained.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-44c5601e.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="historical-background">HISTORICAL BACKGROUND<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#historical-background" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>First aid was being practical from ancient times. It was the famous surgeon who was the first to conceive the idea of first aid. He was General Esmarch (1823-1908).</p>
<p>In 1877 St John Ambulance Association of England was formed. In 1920, The Red Cross society of India was established with more than 400 branches all over India.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symbols-used-in-first-aid">SYMBOLS USED IN FIRST AID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symbols-used-in-first-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The internationally accepted symbol first aid is the white cross on a green background shown below.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a894d529.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="iso-symbol">ISO SYMBOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iso-symbol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Some organizations may make use of the Star of Life, although this is usually reserved for use by ambulance services, or may use symbols such as the Maltese Cross, like the Order of Malta Ambulance Corps and St John Ambulance. Other symbols may also be used.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="st-john-ambulance">St John Ambulance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#st-john-ambulance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cross-of-the-order-of-st-john">CROSS OF THE ORDER OF ST JOHN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cross-of-the-order-of-st-john" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="maltese-or-amalfi-cross">MALTESE OR AMALFI CROSS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maltese-or-amalfi-cross" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>STAR OF LIFE</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-a0b21991.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-red-cross">THE RED CROSS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-red-cross" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-5927706c.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<p>The Red Crescent used in Islamic countries and hold similar disciplinesa Red Cross</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-red-cross-emblem">THE RED CROSS EMBLEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-red-cross-emblem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In 1859 Jean-Henri Dunant witnessed the aftermath of the Battle of Solferino, and his work led to the formation of the Red Cross, with a key stated aim of "aid to sick and wounded soldiers in the field". The Red Cross and Red Crescent are still the largest provider of first aid worldwide.</p>
<p>St John Ambulance historical back ground</p>
<p>While ST John's Ambulance is registered in 42 countries, Eleven priorities of St John ambulance currently exist:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>England and The Islands</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scotland</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Australia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Canada New Zealand</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>South Africa</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>United States of America</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wales</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>St John Kenya</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>St John Singapore</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hong Kong</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>St John Ambulance is a trade name used by a number of affiliated organizations in different countries, counties, states or provinces dedicated to the teaching and practice of <strong>medical first aid</strong> and the provision of <strong>ambulance</strong> and community volunteer services, all of which derive their origins from the <strong>St John Ambulance Association</strong> founded in 1877 in the <strong>United Kingdom</strong>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="st-john-and-the-industrial-revolution">St John and the Industrial revolution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#st-john-and-the-industrial-revolution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Britain was one of the first countries to become industrial and in the 19th century there were many dangerous workplaces. Conditions and machinery were hazardous and workers were exhausted by the long hours. Accidents were frequent but workers rarely saw a doctor in time. <strong>Death</strong> or <strong>disability</strong> from untreated injuries was common.</p>
<p>Members of the British Order wanted to find a way to help. They decided to train ordinary people in first aid so accident victims could be treated quickly and on the spot, and in 1877 they set up St John Ambulance to do this. Classes were set up across the country, particularly in workplaces and areas of heavy industry, but also in villages, seaside towns and middle class suburbs.</p>
<p>During The 20th century, when the National Health Service was founded, there were far fewer doctors and hospital beds than today, St John nurses looked after the sick and injured in their own homes.</p>
<p>The St John Ambulance Association and The St John Ambulance Brigade were amalgamated in 1974 to form the present <strong>St John Ambulance Foundation</strong>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-first-aid">OBJECTIVES OF FIRST AID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-first-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To save life</li>
<li>To control adverse effects of injury.</li>
<li>To ease the Pain-to reduce Pain.</li>
</ul>
<p>To avoid further injury.
Prepare for medical treatment
To assist the doctor.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scope-of-first-aid-3ps">SCOPE OF FIRST AID-3PS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scope-of-first-aid-3ps" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One set of goals of first aid is called the "Three P's":</p>
<ul>
<li>Preserve life</li>
<li>Promote recovery</li>
<li>Prevent the condition from worsening</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preserve-life">PRESERVE LIFE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preserve-life" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Help to stop bleeding</li>
<li>Treat injuries in the right order-(triage)</li>
<li>Maintain airway open and clear</li>
<li>Perform CPR (when there is no breathing and no pulse)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevent-further-injury">PREVENT FURTHER INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevent-further-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dress wound to prevent infection</li>
<li>Provide comfort to casualty</li>
<li>Place casualty in a comfortable position and stop the person from being injured even more.</li>
<li>Stop the condition worsening e.g. a fracture. If possible, an injured person should not be moved.</li>
</ul>
<p>First aid include how to safely move injured people — or move them anyway with less harm if there is no choice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="promote-recovery">PROMOTE RECOVERY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#promote-recovery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Relieve casualty from anxiety</li>
<li>Relieve pain and discomfort</li>
<li>Handle casualty gently</li>
<li>Protect casualty from cold and wet conditions</li>
<li>Reassure casualty</li>
</ul>
<p>"</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-role-of-a-first-aider">THE ROLE OF A FIRST AIDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-a-first-aider" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The person who renders emergency service on the spot until the medical aid is obtained.</p>
<p>A sound knowledge based on first aid enables a rescuer to give skilled services during accidents and sudden illness to;</p>
<ul>
<li>preserve life</li>
<li>promote recovery</li>
<li>Prevent injury or illness being aggravated until the medical aid has been obtained.</li>
</ul>
<p>The role of a first aider is to give someone help, while making sure that they and anyone else involved are safe and that they don't make the situation worse.</p>
<p>These are the seven Roles one need to fulfill as a first aider during an emergency:</p>
<ol>
<li>Assess the situation quickly and calmly:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Safety:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are you or they in any danger?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is it safe for you to go up to them?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scene: What caused the accident or situation?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How many casualties are there?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Situation: What's happened?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>How many people are involved and how old are they?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What do you think the main injuries could be?</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Protect yourself, casualty and bystanders from any danger:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Always protect yourself first - never put yourself at risk</li>
<li>Only move them to safety if leaving them would cause them more harm.eg removing a casualty from the road</li>
<li>If you can't make an area safe, call 999/112 for emergency help</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Prevent infection between you and casualty:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Wash your hands or use alcohol gel</li>
<li>Wear disposable gloves</li>
<li>Don't touch an open wound without gloves on</li>
<li>Don't breathe, cough or sneeze over a wound or a casualty—use a face mask</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Comfort and reassure:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Stay calm and take charge of the situation</li>
<li>Introduce yourself to them to help gain their trust</li>
<li>Explain what's happening and why</li>
<li>Say what you're going to do, before you do it—obtain consent from casualty</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Assess the casualty:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>If there's more than one casualty, help those with life-threatening conditions first.! —ABC approach</li>
<li>Start with the Primary Survey and deal with any life-threatening conditions</li>
<li>Then, if you've dealt with these successfully, move on to the Secondary Survey</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Give first aid treatment:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Prioritize the most life threatening conditions:</li>
<li>Then move on to less serious ones</li>
<li>Get help from others if possible</li>
</ul>
<p>The 5 Bs go along with the ABCs to help you prioritize care. If there are several people injured, the 5Bs can help you to decide who to treat first:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Breathing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>bleeding</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>burns</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>bones</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>bites s</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Arrange for the right kind of help:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Call helpline or for an ambulance if you think it's serious</li>
<li>Take or send them to hospital if it's a serious condition but is unlikely to get worse</li>
<li>For a less serious condition call for medical advice.</li>
<li>Suggest they see their doctor if they're concerned about a less serious condition</li>
<li>Advise them to go home to rest, but to seek help if they feel worse</li>
<li>Stay with them until you can leave them in the right care.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="multiple-casualties">MULTIPLE CASUALTIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#multiple-casualties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Be sure to assess all casualties.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safety-first">SAFETY FIRST!<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safety-first" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Those making noise are likely to survive. THEY ARE BREATHING</li>
<li>Look for those who are SILENT</li>
<li>NOT BREATHING</li>
<li>SHOCK</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="golden-rules">GOLDEN RULES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#golden-rules" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Be calm,</li>
<li>Quick</li>
<li>Methodical and find out all major injuries.</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Stoppage of breathing-, start artificial respiration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Try to stop bleeding.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevent shock if present and shift to nearby hospital. Do not allow a patient with shock to go home alone</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keep the patient warm. And avoid shock</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not move unnecessarily</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do only what is necessary.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reassure the casualty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid crowed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allow fresh air</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be careful removing his clothes, do not hurt the casualty</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Quickest means of transport at emergency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For serious accidents inform police.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-principles-and-rules-of-first-aid">BASIC PRINCIPLES AND RULES OF FIRST AID<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-principles-and-rules-of-first-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Obtain a correct detailed history of the incident or accident</li>
<li>Observe and examine thoroughly and note every symptom.</li>
<li>Treat the casualty as per the diagnosis until the doctor arrives or patient is shifted to the nearby hospital.</li>
<li>IF the accident is at home - call neighbor, if the accident is at the public place call police</li>
<li>Keep phone numbers of doctor, police control room.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="responsibilities-what-a-first-aider-should-do-in-an-emergency">RESPONSIBILITIES: WHAT A FIRST AIDER SHOULD DO IN AN EMERGENCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#responsibilities-what-a-first-aider-should-do-in-an-emergency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Assess the situation QUICKLY – Scene safe, get help and protect yourself, others, and casualty from danger</li>
<li>Make a diagnosis</li>
<li>Provide treatment</li>
<li>Arrange for removal to hospital</li>
<li>Prevent cross infection in so far as possible</li>
<li>Make report for the Emergency Services</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emergency-services-call">Emergency Services call<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-services-call" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Phone number you are calling from, CALL HELPLINE</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Location</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Incident/Accident</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Other Services</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Number of casualties</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Extent of the injury or illness</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>PRIMARY SURVEY or PATIENT ASSESSMENT:</strong>.
Rescue breath purpose: to find out if air way is clear and to send oxygen to the lungs</p>
<p>The Primary Survey is a quick way for you to find out if someone has any injuries or conditions which are life-threatening. If you follow each step methodically, you can identify each life-threatening condition and deal with it in order of priority.</p>
<p>DRS ABC used to remember the steps:</p>
<ul>
<li>Danger</li>
<li>To yourself</li>
<li>Others</li>
<li>casualty</li>
<li>Response</li>
<li>Send for help</li>
<li>Airway</li>
<li>Breathing</li>
<li>Circulation.</li>
</ul>
<p>You'll need to go through the Primary Survey every time you help someone, and make sure you don't get distracted by anything else. Only move onto the <strong>Secondary Survey</strong>, if you've already done the Primary Survey and succeeded in dealing with any life-threatening conditions</p>
<p>&gt; Danger:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If someone needs help, before you go up to them check – is it safe?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No: If you can see or hear any danger nearby, for you or them, like broken glass or oncoming traffic, then make the situation safe before you get any closer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Yes: If you can't see or hear any danger then it is safe to go up to them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Send for help; Incase of accidents; call help line for serious medical emergencies</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Are there any dangers to casualty-remove the danger e.g. switch off any electric cable</p>
<ul>
<li>R=response. Levels of response</li>
<li>A = Airway – is the air way open?, clear, blocked?</li>
<li>B = Breathing – Is the patient breathing? Look, Listen, Feel</li>
<li>C = Circulation – Signs of circulation or severe bleeding?</li>
</ul>
<p>Response levels</p>
<ul>
<li>A = Alert, aware,</li>
<li>V = Voice, verbal response</li>
<li>P = Pain, response to pain</li>
<li>U = Unresponsive casualty, unconscious</li>
</ul>
<p>Unconsciousness or an altered conscious state be caused by</p>
<ul>
<li>Direct injury or illness affecting the brain</li>
<li>Lack of oxygen to the brain</li>
<li>Poisons and toxic products in the blood</li>
</ul>
<p>THE AIRWAY</p>
<p>How to clear and or open the airways</p>
<ul>
<li>Tilt head backwards</li>
<li>Turn mouth slightly downwards to allow drainage of foreign material</li>
<li>Clear foreign material with your fingers, if required. Only remove dentures if they are loose or broken</li>
<li>With infant in the recovery position, clear mouth of foreign material with little finger.</li>
</ul>
<p>WHAT TO DO IF SOMEONE IS UNRESPONSIVE AND NOT BREATHING NORMALLY.</p>
<ul>
<li>Open their airway</li>
<li>Tilt head</li>
<li>Check for normal breathing for up to 10 seconds</li>
<li>If they're breathing normally: Put them in the recovery position</li>
<li>Then call for emergency helpline</li>
<li>If they're not breathing call for emergency helpline Start CPR.</li>
<li>find an AED</li>
<li>Give two rescue breaths.</li>
<li>Pump Give 30 Chest compressions at a rate of 100– 120 per minute Continue to pump and give rescue breaths until help arrives.</li>
</ul>
<p>SECONDARY SURVEY VITAL SIGNS:</p>
<p>Breathing – Rhythm, Rate: Adult 12 – 20 per min, Child 15 – 30 per min, Infant 25 – 50 per min</p>
<p>Pulse – Rhythm, Rate: Adult 60 – 80 per min, Child 70 – 150 per min, Infant 100 – 160 per min</p>
<p>Skin – Color, Temperature, Moisture</p>
<p>History of Casualty:</p>
<ul>
<li>S = Signs and Symptoms</li>
<li>A = Allergies</li>
<li>M = Medications, medical bracelet, medical ID jewellery</li>
<li>P = Pertinent past history</li>
<li>L = Last oral intake</li>
<li>E = Events leading to injury or illness</li>
</ul>
<p>HEAD TO TOE EXAM: DOTS</p>
<p>Always start at the head and work to the toes using dots method</p>
<ul>
<li>D.DEFORMITY</li>
<li>O; OPEN WOUNDS</li>
<li>T; TENDERNESS</li>
<li>S; SEWLLING</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Head = DOTS,</li>
<li>Eyes – Pupils Equal Round, unequal pupils</li>
<li>Mouth – odd breath odours, teeth,</li>
<li>Neck = DOTS of spine area,</li>
<li>Chest = DOTS, equal expansion of chest and use of accessory muscles</li>
<li>Abdomen = DOTS</li>
<li>Lower back = DOTS of lumber's spine area</li>
<li>Pelvis = DOTS, bodily fluids</li>
<li>Legs &amp; feet = DOTS, pulses,</li>
<li>Arms &amp; hands = DOTS, pulses,</li>
<li>Medical ID bracelet, needle marks, insulin pens, inhalers etc</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recovery-position">RECOVERY POSITION:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recovery-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Kneel beside the casualty, remove spectacles and bulky objects from the pockets</li>
<li>Position nearest arm right angles to body</li>
<li>Raise furthest leg and pull it up until foot is flat on the floor</li>
<li>Bring the back of furthest hand against cheek nearest you</li>
<li>Pull on far leg, roll him towards you, onto his side and adjust leg – knee is bent at right angles</li>
<li>Tilt head back to ensure that the airway remains open</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-447c3957.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recovery-position">Recovery position<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recovery-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dealing-with-an-alert-casualty">DEALING WITH AN ALERT CASUALTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dealing-with-an-alert-casualty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Always communicate with the casualty in a calm, clear and reassuring manner that matches the casualty's level of consciousness.</p>
<p>It is safest to approach a casualty from the feet up to the shoulders to get a response.</p>
<ul>
<li>Check response by touching the casualty on the shoulders and asking, "Hello, are you okay can you hear me?"</li>
<li>Avoid shaking, especially children and infants. In every instance where first aid is to be provided, the casualty's consent is required.</li>
<li>It should be obtained from every conscious, adult deemed competent. The consent may be either oral or written.</li>
</ul>
<p>Permission to render first aid to an unconscious casualty or a casualty deemed incompetent is implied and a first aider should not hesitate to treat an unconscious casualty.</p>
<ul>
<li>build trust in the casualty</li>
<li>in case of diversity and communication-language barrier...look for one who understands the local language</li>
<li>talk first to the parent-get their permission in case of children</li>
<li>children-use shorter phrases</li>
<li>listen carefully</li>
<li>eye contact</li>
<li>calm confident voice</li>
<li>do not speak fast</li>
<li>be concise and,concrite</li>
<li>keep instructions clear and simple, use short sentences and simple words</li>
<li>check that casualty understands what you mean</li>
<li>use hand gestures if necessary</li>
<li>do not interrupt casualty</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Causes of unconsciousness are the life threatening emergencies acronymed as:</p>
<ol>
<li>'F.I.S.H'</li>
<li>'S.H.A.P.P.ED'</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fainting</li>
<li>Infantile convulsions</li>
<li>Shock</li>
<li>Head injury</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li></li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>Stroke</li>
<li>Heart attack</li>
<li>A asphyxia</li>
<li>Poison</li>
<li>Epileptic fits</li>
<li>Diabetes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chain-of-survival">CHAIN OF SURVIVAL:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chain-of-survival" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; Early Access = getting help; an ambulance and AED
&gt; Early CPR = this supplies blood to heart &amp; brain
&gt; Early Defibrillation = a shock may restore the heartbeat
&gt; Early Advanced care = specialized life support treatment</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="infection-prevention">INFECTION PREVENTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#infection-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When giving first aid to a sick or injured person you should try to minimize the risks to yourself, the patient, and any helpers or bystanders.</p>
<p>Ten basic rules for first aid</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>When possible, wash your hands with soap and water and apply disposable latex gloves before touching a wound, blood or other body fluids.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the case of serious bleeding, where there is no time to obtain or apply gloves, it is still possible to control the blood loss without having any direct contact with blood. Place your hands in plastic bags, and use the patient's hands to apply pressure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If you have any cuts or wounds on your hands, ensure that they are fully covered by a waterproof dressing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cover your mouth/nose during any treatment of a patient with a potentially serious infection (e.g. tuberculosis) to avoid inhaling infected droplets.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If you are splashed with blood or other body fluids, wash the area thoroughly with soap and water as soon as possible. Then contact your doctor for specific medical advice.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If any of your clothing has been contaminated by body fluids, remove it promptly and immerse it in a container of household bleach, mixed according to and following the instructions on the label.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Safely dispose of any used dressings, bandages and disposable gloves by placing into a plastic or paper bag, and sealing well before putting it into a rubbish bin or burning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is a hospital or medical clinic nearby, the dressings can be disposed of in a medical Hazardous Waste bin where they will be correctly and incinerated.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Used instruments, such as scissors or splinter forceps, should be cleaned thoroughly under running water. Serrated edges should be scrubbed with a fine nailbrush under running water. The articles should then be disinfected, preferably by immersion in a 1:80 bleach solution.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After removing disposable gloves always wash your hands thoroughly with soap and water. Dry your hands well to avoid cracking of the skin.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Rules for wound care</p>
<p><strong>Wash your hands thoroughly and always apply disposable gloves.</strong></p>
<p>A wound containing dirt or other contaminants should be cleaned with either an antiseptic solution or soap and water. Check the expiry date of any solution you wish to use and DO NOT use if past the expiry date.</p>
<ul>
<li>The wound should be dried thoroughly before the dressing is applied.</li>
<li>Avoid direct finger or hand contact with the wound or the central part of the sterile dressing.</li>
<li>Apply a light dressing to the wound and secure it with a bandage or tape.</li>
<li>If the dressing is accidentally dropped or slips off the wound, apply a fresh one at once.</li>
<li>If the wound has any obvious discharge present, use an absorbent dressing on top of the first sterile dressing and bandage it in place firmly.</li>
<li>After securing the wound dressing, remove your gloves and wrap them with any soiled dressings and put them in a plastic or paper</li>
</ul>
<p>bag. The bag should be placed in a covered disposal bin or in a Hazardous Waste container.</p>
<p><strong>NB.</strong></p>
<p>If contamination with blood occurs, the hands—including the area under the fingernails—should be washed vigorously with soap and water or a mild solution of bleach (about 1 tablespoon of bleach per quart of water, or about 15 milliliters of bleach per liter of water) as soon as possible. If neither is readily available, an alcohol-based hand sanitizer can be used.</p>
<p>Contact with saliva and urine should also be avoided, although these fluids are much less likely to result in disease transmission than is contact with blood</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-25fdd311.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p><strong>INCIDENT MANAGEMENT FOR FIRST AIDERS</strong></p>
<p>Incident management refers to the skills required to manage the scene of an emergency. First aiders may be 'first on scene' at an incident so need to know basic principles of incident management.</p>
<p>The main principle of incident management is that you are the most important person and your safety comes first!</p>
<p>Your first actions when coming across the scene of an incident should be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check for any dangers to yourself or bystanders</li>
<li>Manage any dangers found (if safe to do so)</li>
<li>Ensure continuing safety of yourself and bystanders</li>
</ul>
<p>Imagine you came across an incident think about the following questions</p>
<ul>
<li>What would your first action be</li>
<li>What dangers could there be in this situation</li>
<li>How would you manage these dangers?</li>
<li>Which other emergency?</li>
<li>Services would be required?</li>
</ul>
<p>In some situations it may be too dangerous for you approach the scene. In this situation you should remember that you are the most important person – stay back and call for professional assistance.</p>
<p>Calling for emergency help</p>
<p>In many first aid situations, help from the emergency services may be required.</p>
<p>Ensure you know which number to call!.</p>
<p>Give clear, precise information about</p>
<ul>
<li>The location of the incident</li>
<li>The number of casualties / people involved</li>
<li>The nature of their injuries</li>
<li>In some cases, their age, sex</li>
<li>Any hazards at the incident (e.g: spilt fuel, fire, electricity)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="action-plan">ACTION PLAN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#action-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A.M.E.G.A</p>
<ul>
<li>ASSES</li>
<li>MAKE SAFE</li>
<li>EMERGENCY AID</li>
<li>GET HELP</li>
<li>AFTER CARE</li>
</ul>
<p>ASSES</p>
<ul>
<li>stopp only fools rush in</li>
<li>look (use your eyes ears and nose to smell)</li>
<li>think.(what happened who is involved when did it happen, why did it happen what resources do you have)</li>
</ul>
<p>MAKE SAFE</p>
<ul>
<li>TURN OFF FIRE ENGINES, ELECTRIC, GAS, WATER ETC</li>
<li>INCASE SOMEONE IS ON FIRE, STOP, DROP, AND ROLL</li>
<li>FOR DROWNING, REACH OUT FOR A FLOATER AND THROW TO CASUALTY</li>
<li>ELECTRIC SHOCK - DISCONNECT AT FUSE BOARD</li>
</ul>
<p>EMERGENCY AID</p>
<ul>
<li>given by someone who is qualified this may</li>
<li>include CPR of AR or Hemlich maneuver</li>
</ul>
<p>GETTING HELP</p>
<ul>
<li>DECIDE WHO TO CALL: AMBULANCE POLICE, FIRE GUARD, MINE RESCUE, ELECTRIC BOARD GAS BOARD, AND WATER</li>
<li>GET HELP FROM PUBLIC EG, PUBLIC, TO CONROL TRAFFIC</li>
</ul>
<p>AFTER CARE</p>
<ul>
<li>ANY TREATMENT GIVEN</li>
<li>OBSERVATION ON BREATCHING PULSE, LEVEL OF RESPOSE</li>
<li>MINOR CASESARRANGE FOR A LIFT HOME</li>
</ul>
<p>METHANE</p>
<p>The Emergency services widely use the METHANE acronym to build a report for alerting others about a major incident.</p>
<p>METHANE stands for:</p>
<ul>
<li>Major Incident Declared</li>
<li>Exact location</li>
<li>Type of incident</li>
<li>Hazards</li>
<li>Access</li>
<li>Number and type of casualties</li>
<li>Emergency services present and required</li>
</ul>
<p>METHANE is now the recognized model for passing incident information between services and their control rooms information is shared in a consistent way, quickly and easily between emergency service providers</p>
<p>PRORITIZING THE INCIDENT</p>
<ul>
<li>5BS FOR PROFITZING THE INCIDENT</li>
<li>BREATHING</li>
<li>BLEEDING</li>
<li>BURNS</li>
<li>BONES</li>
<li>BITES</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="accidents">ACCIDENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accidents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An accident is an event, which happens unexpectedly. The extent of the injury depends on various factors. The accidents, which are most likely to come across, are as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li>Wounds</li>
<li>Sprains and dislocations</li>
<li>Fractures (broken bones)</li>
<li>Burns and scalds.</li>
</ul>
<p>Sometimes there may be a history given that the patient has received an injury to the head or some other part of the body but there is no visible injury.</p>
<p>However in these cases the patient may be unconscious, may show signs of shock or may complain of pain. In all such cases you transfer the patient to the Health Center immediately.</p>
<p>As you are a first aider and the aim of your assistance is as follows-</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Prevent immediate danger of death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give artificial respiration, if required</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Guard against shock or treat for shock.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not remove clothing unnecessarily.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reassure the patient and relieve pain.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Arrange for removal of the patient to the nearest HOSPITAL</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e0e8875c.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="traffic-accidents-clapp">TRAFFIC ACCIDENTS-CLAPP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#traffic-accidents-clapp" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>C – Control the situation
L – Look for hazards
A – Assess the situation
P – Protect
P- Prioritize</p>
<p>The first aid acronym CLAPP is a way to think about initial accident scene management.</p>
<p>Control the situation - Stop take a breath and take charge of people and traffic</p>
<p>Look for hazards – Look for anything that might cause harm to children or bystanders in the immediate area. Don’t forget yourself!</p>
<p>Assess the situation – Gather as much information as possible about what has occurred from bystanders and try to make a diagnosis (history, signs and symptoms)</p>
<p>Protect and prioritise – Ensure protection is worn (gloves) and the casualties are prioritised using a Triage system. Try to gain assistance from a bystander and contact the emergency services.</p>
<p>Give emergency services by prioritizing!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-servey-d-r-s-a-b-cd">PRIMARY SERVEY-D R S A B CD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-servey-d-r-s-a-b-cd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Before attempting first aid you should always:</p>
<ul>
<li>D...check that you are safe, any <strong>danger</strong> to you or casualty</li>
<li>R...check for a <strong>response</strong></li>
<li>A...open the casualty’s <strong>airway</strong> if necessary</li>
<li>B...check to see if the casualty is <strong>breathing</strong></li>
<li>C...If breathing, check to see if the casualty is <strong>bleeding</strong>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Summarized as: “DRSABC D”</p>
<ul>
<li>Danger</li>
<li>Response</li>
<li>Airway</li>
<li>Breathing</li>
<li>C...Circulation Check for severe BLEEDING, Carotid or radius pulse</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abc-of-life-threats-to-abc-life-needs">ABC OF LIFE - THREATS TO ABC LIFE NEEDS..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abc-of-life-threats-to-abc-life-needs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>To live we need oxygen to reach the vital organs and especially the BRAIN</li>
<li><strong>The brain must not be without O2 for longer than 3 minutes</strong></li>
<li>Therefore:</li>
<li>A ~ Airway – <strong>open air</strong> way if blocked by foreign matter</li>
<li>B ~ breathing- • <strong>Visual breathing?</strong> • Regular? • Strong? • Wheezing?, gasping?</li>
<li>C ~ Circulation..check for bleeding</li>
</ul>
<p>CIRCULATION? check for pulse...carotid pulse, radius pulse</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-is-it">HOW IS IT?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-is-it" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Regular?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Strong?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fast?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shallow?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>LEAKING?- WHERE IS IT? -TRY TO STOP BLEEDING</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of circulation (Cyanosis)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-survey">Primary survey<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-survey" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unconscious-but-breathing-put-in-recovery-position">UNCONSCIOUS BUT BREATHING-put in 'Recovery position.'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unconscious-but-breathing-put-in-recovery-position" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unresponsive-casualty">UNRESPONSIVE CASUALTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unresponsive-casualty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If they're not breathing for emergency help</li>

<li>Find an AED 3.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="accidents">ACCIDENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#accidents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An accident is an event, which happens unexpectedly. The extent of the injury depends on various factors. The accidents, which are most likely to come across, are as follows.</p>
<ul>
<li>Wounds</li>
<li>Sprains and dislocations</li>
<li>Fractures (broken bones)</li>
<li>Burns and scalds.</li>
</ul>
<p>Sometimes there may be a history given that the patient has received an injury to the head or some other part of the body but there is no visible injury.</p>
<p>However in these cases the patient may be unconscious, may show signs of shock or may complain of pain. In all such cases you transfer the patient to the Health Center immediately.</p>
<p>As you are a first aider and the aim of your assistance is as follows-</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevent immediate danger of death.</li>
<li>Give artificial respiration, if required</li>
<li>Guard against shock or treat for shock.</li>
<li>Do not remove clothing unnecessarily.</li>
<li>Reassure the patient and relieve pain.</li>
<li>Arrange for removal of the patient to the nearest HOSPITAL</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-f17e955d.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg"></p>
<p>TRAFFIC ACCIDENTS-CLAPP
C – Control the situation
L – Look for hazards
A – Assess the situation
P – Protect</p>
<p>P- Prioritize</p>
<p>The first aid acronym CLAPP is a way to think about initial accident scene management.</p>
<p>Control the situation - Stop take a breath and take charge of people and traffic</p>
<p>Look for hazards – Look for anything that might cause harm to children or bystanders in the immediate area. Don’t forget yourself!</p>
<p>Assess the situation – Gather as much information as possible about what has occurred from bystanders and try to make a diagnosis (history, signs and symptoms)</p>
<p>Protect and prioritise – Ensure protection is worn (gloves) and the casualties are prioritised using a Triage system. Try to gain assistance from a bystander and contact the emergency services. Give emergency services by prioritizing!</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-2-cadiopulmonary-resustation">UNIT 2; CADIOPULMONARY RESUSTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-2-cadiopulmonary-resustation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Perform CPR to an adult, child and infant</li>
<li>Perform CPR to a drowning victim</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="cadiopulmonarly-resustation">CADIOPULMONARLY RESUSTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cadiopulmonarly-resustation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Another set of goals for keeping a badly hurt person alive is sometimes called "C-A-B" -DRCAB</p>
<p>&gt; ‘keep blood inside the body and the heart beating’</p>
<p>CPR is as easy as
C-A-B</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-6b3ed488.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg">
Compressions Push hard and fast on the center of the victim's chest</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-91032fc6.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
Airway Tilt the victim's head back and lift the chin to open the airway</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-ae642d7f.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg">
Breathing Give mouth-to-mouth rescue breaths</p>
<p>American Heart Association</p>
<p>©2010 American Heart Association 10/10DS3849</p>
<p>Learn and Live</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-someone-is-unconscious-and-breathing">. IF SOMEONE IS UNCONSCIOUS AND BREATHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-someone-is-unconscious-and-breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If a person is unconscious but is breathing and has no other life-threatening conditions, they should be placed in the recovery position until help arrives</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-someone-is-unconscious-and-not-breathing">IF SOMEONE IS UNCONSCIOUS AND NOT BREATHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-someone-is-unconscious-and-not-breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If a person is not breathing normally after an incident, call for an ambulance and start CPR straight away. Mouth to Mouth respiration rate at 16/min</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-d4725fed.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg"></p>
<p>A "cardiac arrest" is when your heart stops beating. This is not the same as a "heart attack", although a heart attack may lead to a cardiac arrest. There are numerous causes of cardiac arrests, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>A disturbance in the heart rhythm</li>
<li>Drugs/poisoning</li>
<li>Heart disease / a heart attack</li>
<li>Traumatic injury/blood loss</li>
<li>Anaphylaxis</li>
</ul>
<p>If a cardiac arrest occurs, blood will stop circulating around the body. Breathing will also cease as well though it may not stop completely for several minutes.</p>
<p>Without a supply of oxygen, brain cells in the start to die in about 3 – 5 minutes leading to brain damage and death.</p>
<p>The purpose of CPR is to keep oxygenated blood flowing around the body to keep the vital organs alive. CPR itself will not restart someone's heart; it just keeps them alive until a defibrillator arrives. A defibrillator is a device which delivers an electrical shock to the heart to restart it.</p>
<p>How help someone who has collapsed</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-770b91f8.jpeg" alt="img-20.jpeg"></p>
<p>DRS ABC to remember what to do:</p>
<ul>
<li>Danger: Check for any dangers to yourself. Response: Check for a response from the casualty.</li>
<li>Send for help</li>
<li>Airway: open their airway</li>
<li>Breathing: Check for normal breathing (regular breaths) for up to 10 seconds</li>
</ul>
<p>Compressions: If the casualty is not breathing, you should call an ambulance and start chest compressions.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Once you've found someone isn't breathing, and there is no circulation you should start CPR straight by administering 30 chest compressions...</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Send for AED. (Automated external defibrillator): An AED is reliable, safe, computerized device that delivers electric shocks to a casualty in cardiac arrest when the ECG rhythm is one that is likely to respond to a shock. Simplicity of operation is a key feature: controls are kept to a minimum, 'voice and visual prompts' guide rescuers.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>After 30 chest compressions, you should give 2 rescue breaths. You should aim for a rate of 100 – 120 chest compressions a minute.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-ab369152.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p>In order for the heart to be restarted, it may require an electrical shock from a defibrillator or drugs given by a paramedic/doctor. However, good quality chest compressions will significantly increase the chance of the defibrillator being able to restart the heart.</p>
<p>You should only stop doing CPR if:</p>
<p>A defibrillator arrives and is about to be used
The casualty shows signs of life: coughing, breathing etc.</p>
<ul>
<li>You are asked to stop by a healthcare professional (ambulance crew etc.)</li>
</ul>
<p>'Ideally, you should only carry out CPR for a couple of minutes before swapping with someone else. This is to ensure that the chest compressions remain of good quality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>INFANT CPR—rescue breathing'</p>
<ul>
<li>: use 2 fingers for; 30 compressions</li>
<li>PUBERTY CHILD</li>
<li>rescue breathing'</li>
<li>30 compressions; use one palm hand heel</li>
<li>2 rescue breaths</li>
<li>30;2</li>
<li>remember pocket breathing mask/face shield for protection</li>
<li>never use AED on infants under one year</li>
</ul>
<p>For Cardiac arrest use DRCAB procedure. This is because the heart has stopped and there is no circulation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit3-emergency-situations">UNIT3; EMERGENCY SITUATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit3-emergency-situations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Conditions that require first aid emergencies priorities</li>
<li>Manage casualties and apply first aid skill So relieve choking</li>
<li>Management of various medical emergencies condition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conditions-that-require-first-aid-emergencies-priorities">CONDITIONS THAT REQUIRE FIRST AID EMERGENCIES PRIORITIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-that-require-first-aid-emergencies-priorities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">INTRODUCTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first priority is to save lives. A person who is unconscious and unresponsive may be close to death, and rescuers must assess the situation and begin treatment as needed, to maintain the ABCs: a person's airway (A), breathing (B), and circulation (C). A problem in any of these areas may be fatal if not corrected quickly.</p>
<p>The airway, which is the passage through which air travels to the lungs, can become blocked (for example, by choking on or inhaling a piece of food). Many disorders, such as emphysema and asthma, can make breathing difficult.</p>
<p>Circulation of blood, which depends on a pumping and beating heart muscle, can stop during cardiac arrest, in which case cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR) is necessary.</p>
<p>The next priority is to get medical assistance by calling for emergency medical care, except when people experience:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cardiac arrest</li>
<li>Choking</li>
</ul>
<p>When a person's heart stops or a person is choking, treatment should be started before calling for help. The caller should not hang up until told to do so. If several lay people (rescuers) are present, one should call for help while another begins assessment and first aid.</p>
<p>Before calling for medical assistance, rescuers should provide:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cardiopulmonary resuscitation (CPR)</li>
<li>Maneuvers to relieve choking (for example, abdominal thrusts, also called the Heimlich maneuver)</li>
</ul>
<p>If many people are injured, the most seriously injured person should be treated first. Assessment should take less than 1 minute per</p>
<p>injured person. In each case, the rescuer should consider whether the situation is:</p>
<ul>
<li>Life threatening</li>
<li>Urgent but not life threatening</li>
<li>Not urgent</li>
</ul>
<p>Determining who is in most urgent need of treatment may be difficult, but someone screaming in pain may be less seriously injured than someone who cannot breathe or who is in a coma and, therefore, quiet. Difficulty breathing and massive bleeding are life threatening, but a broken hand or foot can almost always wait for treatment, no matter how painful.</p>
<p>When there are many people with serious injuries and resources are limited, rescuers may need to provide treatment only to those people who rescuers believe have a chance of surviving.</p>
<p>When injured people are unable to convey medical information because they are confused or unconscious or because of the severity of their condition, the information should be obtained in other ways. For example, if an unconscious person is found near an empty bottle of pills, the bottle should be given to the emergency medical personnel. A description of how a person became injured and other information from bystanders, family members, or rescuers can be essential to the person's treatment. After these steps have been taken, reassurance and simple measures, such as supplying a blanket and keeping the person calm and warm, can provide comfort.</p>
<p><strong>LIST OF CONDITIONS THAT OFTEN REQUIRE FIRST AID EMERGENCY</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cardiac Arrest, which will lead to death unless CPR preferably combined with an AED is started within minutes. There is often no time to wait for the emergency services to arrive as 92 percent of people suffering a sudden cardiac arrest die before reaching hospital according to the American Heart Association.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Choking, blockage of the airway which can quickly result in death due to lack of oxygen if the patient's trachea is not cleared, for example by the Heimlich Maneuver.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Childbirth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Altitude sickness, which can begin in susceptible people at altitudes as low as 5,000 feet, can cause potentially fatal swelling of the brain or lungs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anaphylaxis, a life-threatening condition in which the airway can become constricted and the patient may go into shock. The reaction can be caused by a systemic allergic reaction to allergens such as insect bites or peanuts. Anaphylaxis is initially treated with injection of epinephrine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Battlefield first aid—This protocol refers to treating, gunshot wounds, burns, bone fractures, etc. as seen either in the 'traditional' battlefield setting or in an area subject to damage by large-scale weaponry, such as a bomb blast.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bone fracture, a break in a bone initially treated by stabilizing the fracture with a splint.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Burns, which can result in damage to tissues and loss of body fluids through the burn site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diving disorders, drowning or asphyxiation..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Heart attack, or inadequate blood flow to the blood vessels supplying the heart muscle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Heat stroke, also known as sunstroke or hyperthermia, which tends to occur during heavy exercise in high humidity, or with inadequate water, though it may occur spontaneously in some chronically ill persons. Sunstroke, especially when the victim has been unconscious, often causes major damage to body systems such as brain, kidney, liver, gastric</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>tract. Unconsciousness for more than two hours usually leads to permanent disability. Emergency treatment involves rapid cooling of the patient.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Heavy bleeding, treated by applying pressure (manually and later with a pressure bandage) to the wound site and elevating the limb if possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hyperglycemia (diabetic coma) and Hypoglycemia (insulin shock).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypothermia, or Exposure, occurs when a person's core body temperature falls below 33.7 °C (92.6 °F). First aid for a mildly hypothermic patient includes rewarming, which can be achieved by wrapping the affected person in a blanket, and providing warm drinks, such as soup, and high energy food, such as chocolate. However, rewarming a severely hypothermic person could result in a fatal arrhythmia, an irregular heart rhythm.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insect and animal bites and stings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Joint dislocation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poisoning, which can occur by injection, inhalation, absorption, or ingestion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Seizures, or a malfunction in the electrical activity in the brain. Three types of seizures include a grand mal (which usually features convulsions as well as temporary respiratory abnormalities, change in skin complexion, etc.) and petit mal (which usually features twitching, rapid blinking, and/or fidgeting as well as altered consciousness and temporary respiratory abnormalities).</p>
</li>
<li>
