<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-do-for-a-closed-fracture">WHAT TO DO FOR A CLOSED FRACTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do-for-a-closed-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Advise the casualty to keep still. Support the joints above and below the injury with your hands until it is immobilized with a sling or bandages, in the position in which it is found.</li>
<li>Place padding around the injury for extra support. Take or send the casualty to the hospital; a casualty with an arm injury may be transported by car; call 911 for emergency help for a leg injury.</li>
<li>For firmer support and/or if removal to the hospital is likely to be delayed, secure the injured part to an unaffected part of the</li>
</ol>
<p>body. For upper limb fractures, immobilize the arm with a sling. For lower limb fractures, move the uninjured leg to the injured one and secure with broad-fold bandages. Always tie knots on the uninjured side.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Treat for shock if necessary. Do not raise an injured leg. Elevate an uninjured limb if shock is present. Monitor and record vital signs while waiting for help. Check the circulation beyond a sling or bandage (p.243) every ten minutes. If the circulation is impaired, loosen the bandages.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="open-wound-fracture">OPEN WOUND FRACTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#open-wound-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aims">AIMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To prevent blood loss, movement, and infection at the site of injury</li>
<li>To arrange removal to the hospital, with comfortable support</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-do-for-an-open-fracture">WHAT TO DO FOR AN OPEN FRACTURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do-for-an-open-fracture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Cover the wound with a sterile dressing or large, clean, gauze pad. Apply pressure around the injury to control bleeding; be careful not to press on a protruding bone.</li>
<li>Carefully place a sterile wound dressing or more clean padding over and around the dressing.</li>
<li>Secure the dressing and padding with a bandage. Bandage firmly, but not so tightly that it impairs the circulation beyond the bandage.</li>
<li>Immobilize the injured part as for a closed fracture, and arrange to transport the casualty to the hospital</li>
<li>Treat the casualty for shock if necessary. Do not raise the injured leg. Monitor and record vital signs—level of response, breathing, and pulse—while waiting for help to arrive. Check the circulation beyond the bandage every ten minutes. If the circulation is impaired, loosen the bandages.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specialcase-protruding-bone">SPECIALCASE: PROTRUDING BONE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specialcase-protruding-bone" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If a bone end is protruding, build up pads of clean, soft, nonfluffy material around the bone, until you can bandage over it without pressing on the injury</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dislocated-joint">DISLOCATED JOINT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dislocated-joint" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a joint injury in which the bones are partially or completely pulled out of their normal position. Dislocation can be caused by a strong force wrenching the bone into an abnormal position, or by violent muscle contraction. This very painful injury most often affects the shoulder, knee, jaw, or joints in the thumbs or fingers. Dislocations may be associated with torn ligaments, or with damage to the synovial membrane that lines the joint capsule. Joint dislocation can have serious consequences. If vertebrae are dislocated, the spinal cord can be damaged. Dislocation of the shoulder or hip may damage the large nerves that supply the limbs and result in partial paralysis. A dislocation of any joint may also fracture the bones involved. It is difficult to distinguish a dislocation from a closed fracture. If you are in any doubt, treat the injury as a fracture.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recognition">RECOGNITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recognition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There may be:</p>
<p>I. "Sickening," severe pain
II. Inability to move the joint
III. Swelling and bruising around the affected joint
IV. Shortening, bending or deformity of the area</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="your-aims">YOUR AIMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#your-aims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To prevent movement at the injury site.</li>
<li>To arrange removal to the hospital, with comfortable support.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-to-do">WHAT TO DO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I. If, for example, the casualty has a dislocated shoulder, advise the casualty to keep still. Help him support the injured arm in the position he finds most comfortable.</p>
<p>II. Immobilize the injured arm with a sling.</p>
<p>III. For extra support for an injured arm, secure the limb to the chest by tying a broad-fold bandage around the chest and the sling.</p>
<p>IV. Arrange to take or send the casualty to the hospital. Treat for shock if necessary. Monitor and record vital signs—level of response, breathing, and pulse—while waiting for help.</p>
<p>V. Check the circulation beyond the bandages every ten minutes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caution">CAUTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do not try to replace a dislocated bone into its socket because this may cause further injury.</li>
<li>Do not move the casualty until the injured part is secured and supported, unless she is in immediate danger.</li>
<li>For a hand or arm injury remove bracelets, rings, and watches in case of swelling.</li>
<li>Do not allow the casualty to eat or drink because an anesthetic may be needed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="head-injury">HEAD INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#head-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Head injuries are common. They are potentially serious because they can lead to damage to the brain. There may also be injuries to the spine in the neck, scalp wounds and/or a skull fracture. If a casualty has sustained a minor injury such as a bruise or scalp wound, he is likely to be fully conscious. If he has suffered a more serious blow to the head, such as in a sporting impact, consciousness may be temporarily impaired. The brain lies inside the skull, cushioned by fluid and can therefore be shaken by a blow to the head. This is called</p>
<p>concussion and it often produces a temporary loss of consciousness. Complications from concussion may affect thinking, language, or emotions, and may lead to problems with communication and memory, and cause personality changes, depression, and early-onset dementia. If a casualty has suffered a severe blow to his head, this may cause bleeding or swelling inside the skull that can press on the brain (compression). This is a serious condition. The pressure can rise immediately after the impact or it may develop a few hours or even days later. The severity of the head injury is related to the mechanism of injury and its impact on the head. A serious head injury is likely after a high speed motor collision or a fall from a height.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caution">CAUTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Seek medical advice if you notice signs of a worsening head injury such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Increasing drowsiness</li>
<li>Persistent headache</li>
<li>Confusion, dizziness, balance problems, and/or memory loss</li>
<li>Difficulty speaking</li>
<li>Difficulty walking</li>
<li>Vomiting episodes after the injury</li>
<li>Double vision</li>
<li>aSeizure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-head-injury">Causes of head injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-head-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The brain can be literally "shaken" inside the skull with concussion. Injury that results in bleeding can cause pressure to build up inside the skull and damage the tissues of the brain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessing-the-level-of-consciousness">ASSESSING THE LEVEL OF CONSCIOUSNESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessing-the-level-of-consciousness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Assess a casualty's level of consciousness using the AVPU scale. Check the casualty at regular intervals. Make a note of your findings at each assessment, paying particular attention to any change—the casualty's condition may improve or deteriorate while you are looking after him.</p>
<p>A—Is the casualty Alert? Are his eyes open and does he respond to questions?</p>
<p>V—Does the casualty respond to Voice? Can he answer simple questions and obey commands?</p>
<p>P—Does the casualty respond to Pain? Does he move or open his eyes if pinched?</p>
<p>U—Is he Unresponsive to any stimulus?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recognition">RECOGNITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recognition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There may be:</p>
<ul>
<li>Brief period of impaired consciousness</li>
<li>Scalp wound</li>
<li>Dizziness or nausea</li>
<li>Loss of memory of events at the time of, or immediately preceding the injury</li>
<li>Mild generalized headache</li>
<li>Confusion</li>
</ul>
<p>For severe head injury there may also be:</p>
<ul>
<li>History of a severe blow to the head</li>
<li>Deteriorating level of response</li>
<li>Loss of consciousness</li>
<li>Leakage of blood or blood-stained watery fluid from the ears or nose</li>
<li>Unequal pupil size</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-do">WHAT TO DO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Sit the casualty down and give him a cold compress to hold against the injury. Carry out an assessment of the casualty's level of consciousness using the AVPU scale (opposite). Treat any scalp wounds by applying direct pressure to the wound.</li>
<li>Regular monitor and record vital signs—breathing, pulse and level of response. Watch especially for changes in his level of response</li>
<li>When the casualty has recovered, ask a responsible person to look after him.</li>
<li>If a casualty's injury is the result of a sporting accident, do not allow him to return to the sport until he has been fully assessed by a medical practitioner.</li>
<li>Advise the casualty to seek medical help or arrange transportation to a hospital if he develops signs and symptoms of a worsening head injury, or if ANY of the following apply:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>He is over 65 years of age</li>
<li>He has had previous brain surgery</li>
<li>He is taking anticoagulant (anticlotting) medication</li>
<li>The head injury is accompanied by drug or alcohol intoxication</li>
<li>There is no responsible person to look after him</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="special-case-severe-head-injury">SPECIAL CASE SEVERE HEAD INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#special-case-severe-head-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Call 911 for emergency help—tell the dispatcher that you suspect head injury. Maintain an open and clear airway. Do this in the position the casualty was found—try not to move him because of the additional risk of spinal injury. If this is not possible, use the jaw thrust method to open the airway. Regularly monitor and record vital signs—breathing, pulse, and level of response—while waiting for help to arrive. Watch especially for changes in his level of response</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="crush-injury">CRUSH INJURY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#crush-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Traffic accidents and building site collapses are the most common causes of crush injuries. Other possible causes include explosions, earthquakes, and train crashes. A crush injury may include a fracture,</p>
<p>swelling, and internal bleeding. The crushing force may cause impaired circulation, resulting in numbness at or below the site of injury. You may not detect a pulse in a crushed limb.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caution">CAUTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do not release a casualty who has been crushed for more than 15 minutes.</li>
<li>Do not lift heavy objects.</li>
<li>Do not allow the casualty to eat or drink because an anesthetic may be needed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">AIM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To obtain specialist medical aid urgently, taking any steps possible to treat the casualty</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dangers-of-prolonged-crushing">DANGERS OF PROLONGED CRUSHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dangers-of-prolonged-crushing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the casualty is trapped for any length of time, two serious complications may result. First, prolonged crushing may cause extensive damage to body tissues, especially to muscles. Once the pressure is removed, shock may develop rapidly as tissue fluid leaks into the injured area. More dangerous, toxic substances build up in damaged muscle tissue around a crush injury. If released suddenly into the circulation, these toxins may cause the heart to experience a life-threatening rhythm disturbance first or kidney failure later. This process, called "crush syndrome," is extremely serious and can be fatal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-do">WHAT TO DO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>If you know the casualty has been crushed for less than 15 minutes and you can release him, do this as quickly as possible. Control external bleeding and steady and support any suspected fracture. Treat the casualty for shock but do not raise his legs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the casualty has been crushed for more than 15 minutes, or you cannot move the cause of injury, leave him in the position found and comfort and reassure him.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Call 911 for emergency help, giving clear details of the incident to the dispatcher.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitor and record vital signs—level of response, breathing, and pulse—while waiting for help to arrive.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="eye-wound">EYE WOUND<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#eye-wound" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The eye can be bruised or cut by direct blows or by sharp, chipped fragments of metal, grit, and glass. All eye injuries are potentially serious because of the risk to the casualty's vision. Even superficial abrasions to the surface (cornea) of the eye can lead to scarring or infection, with the possibility of permanent deterioration of vision</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recognition">RECOGNITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recognition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Pain in the eye or eyelids</li>
<li>Visible wound and/or bloodshot appearance</li>
<li>Partial or total loss of vision</li>
<li>Leakage of blood or clear fluid from a wound</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aim">AIM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To prevent further damage</li>
<li>To arrange transportation to the hospital</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caution">CAUTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do not touch or attempt to remove anything that is sticking to, or embedded in, the eyeball or on the colored part (iris) of the eye. Instead, place a paper cup over the affected eye and bandage it in place</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-to-do">WHAT TO DO<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-to-do" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Help the casualty into a half-sitting position or onto on his back, and hold his head to keep it as still as possible. Tell him to keep</li>
</ol>
<p>both eyes still because movement of the “good” eye will cause movement of the injured one, which may damage it further.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Give the casualty a sterile dressing or a clean, nonfluffy pad to hold over the affected eye. If it will take some time to obtain medical help, secure the pad in place with a bandage. Do not apply pressure to the injured eye.</li>
<li>Arrange to take or send the casualty to the hospital</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spinal-injuries">Spinal Injuries:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong> • An injury to the muscles, bones, or nerves associated with the spine. The higher up on the spine it is the more serious the injury will be.</p>
<p><strong>Causes:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Very common in vehicle accidents</li>
<li>Diving in shallow water</li>
<li>Cycling accidents</li>
<li>Any impact, direct or indirect, to these body parts.</li>
<li>Sport accidents such as hockey and football, etc.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-of-injury-and-extent-of-paralysis">Levels of Injury and Extent of Paralysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-injury-and-extent-of-paralysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-2c92b27e.jpeg" alt="img-25.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spinal-injury">Spinal injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Make sure the person doesn't move then get help.</li>
<li>Hold them still. You need to and explain to them that they may have a serious injury and should not move.</li>
<li>If they are unconscious do the CPR steps. Airway and breathing take priority.</li>
<li>Notes: Any time there is a spinal injury you should also suspect a concussion, and visa versa.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="spinal-injury">Spinal injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-symptoms">Signs/symptoms:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mechanism of injury (how it occurred).</li>
<li>Pain, numbness, or paralysis.</li>
<li>Bleeding, swelling, or bruising around the head, ears, or nose.</li>
<li>Unconsciousness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wear safety equipment and wear it properly.</li>
<li>Know the safety rules of sports played.</li>
<li>Use seat belts and car seats.</li>
<li>Avoid alcohol intake when doing physical activity as it impairs sound judgment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="concussion">Concussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong> An injury to the head or the brain. Literally bleeding in the brain or the area around the brain.</p>
<p><strong>Causes:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Any impact, direct or indirect, to the head.</li>
<li>May be associated with a spinal injury.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Signs/Symptoms:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Mechanism of injury.</li>
<li>Pain or numbness.</li>
<li>Bleeding, swelling, or bruising.</li>
<li>Confused.</li>
<li>Loss of memory.</li>
<li>Dizzy.</li>
<li>Ringing in the ears.</li>
<li>Nausea or vomiting.</li>
<li>Unconsciousness.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="concussion">Concussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wear safety equipment and wear it properly.</li>
<li>Know the safety rules of sports played.</li>
<li>Use seat belts and car seats.</li>
<li>Avoid alcohol intake when doing physical activity as it impairs sound judgment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Make sure the person doesn't move.</li>
<li>Hold them still and explain to them that they should not move.</li>
<li>Activate the ambulance right away.</li>
<li>If they are unconscious do the CPR steps but open the airway with a modified jaw thrusts, as opposed to a head tilt.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bandaging">Bandaging:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bandaging is something you would do to control severe bleeding. Ideally you want to use sterile dressings but they may not be readily available so use whatever you have (e.g. towels, clothing). The idea is to put constant pressure over the cut to control bleeding. You want to tie with enough pressure to control the bleeding but not so much so that blood does not get through to the remainder of the limb. If you restrict blood flow that area may die and may require amputation, so be very careful. Once you’ve tied the dressing you need to check to make sure you did not make it too tight, and check this every couple of minutes. For example, if you’ve bandaged a forearm here’s how you check for circulation:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Compare both hands to make sure they are similar in temperature and color.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the hand to make sure it is not swelling or turning blue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask the person if the hand feels numb or tingly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If they lose sensation then it’s too tight. Do not remove the bandage but loosen it a bit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the first dressing becomes soaked with blood then simply put another one on top. Do not remove the original one as you will be reopening the wound.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Notes:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Always use caution when dealing with bodily fluids. Wear gloves and wash your hands immediately after.</li>
<li>Keep in mind that the injured person may go into shock.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="purposes-of-bandage">Purposes of bandage:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purposes-of-bandage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>(1) To secure dressing in position.,
(2) To form slings for support.
(3) To secure pads</p>
<ul>
<li>Roller Bandages: These bandages are made of cotton, gauze crepe, elastic fabric or linen are wrapped around the injured in spiral turns, figure of eight. To improvise, material may be torn into strips of the required length and width.</li>
<li>Width required for finger 2.5 cm</li>
<li>For head and arm 6 cm</li>
<li>For the leg, about 9 cm</li>
<li>For the body 15 cm</li>
<li>The bandages should be tightly and evenly rolled.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bandaging">BANDAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Includes</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Elbow and knee bandaging</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hand and foot bandaging</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tubular bandaging</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Triangular bandaging (scalp bandaging and arm sling)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objective">Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To be able to apply bandages in various locations of the body as indicated</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indications">INDICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To secure dressings</li>
<li>To control bleeding</li>
<li>Give support and immobilization</li>
<li>Reduce swellings in injured parts</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirements">REQUIREMENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A clean tray containing the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Small hand towel</li>
<li>Pair of gloves</li>
<li>Protective mackintosh and draw sheet</li>
<li>Bandaging materials</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Crepe bandage, gauze bandage, gauze roll, firm bandages or other clear improvised material</li>
<li>Roller bandages, tubular bandages and triangular</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Applicator for tubular bandages</li>
<li>Pair of straight scissors</li>
<li>Securing materials: strapping ( or alternatives if strapping not available: safety pins bandage clips)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-bandages">TYPES OF BANDAGES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-bandages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Roller bandages for securing dressings and support injured limbs</li>
<li>Tubular bandages for holding dressings on finger or toes or support injured joints</li>
<li>Triangular bandages used as large dressings, as sling, to secure dressings or immobilize limbs</li>
<li>If bandage not available use improvised materials e.g fabrics like headscarf</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-bandage-application-rules-for-applying-a-bandage">GENERAL BANDAGE APPLICATION/ RULES FOR APPLYING A BANDAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-bandage-application-rules-for-applying-a-bandage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Explain the procedure to the patient while reassuring</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Make the patient comfortable, in a suitable sitting position or when lying down</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the tray beside the patient appropriately</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wash hands and dry them with clean towel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask the assistant to position patient appropriately and in case of a wound or bleeding, fix mackintosh under the injured/part to be bandaged</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In case of a wound or bleeding, put on gloves</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ask patient or assistant to continue supporting the injured</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Work at the front of the patient and from the injured side where possible</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If patient is lying down, pass the bandages under the body's natural hollows/contours at the ankles, knees, waist and neck, then slide the bandages into position by easing them back and forth under the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Apply bandages firmly but not so tightly to avoid interference with circulation in the distal parts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Leave the fingers or toes on a bandaged limb exposed, if possible, so that you can check the circulation afterwards.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use strapping or other securing material to secure the bandage material in position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Where you need to tie, use reef knots to the bandages. Ensure that the knots do not cause discomfort nor pass over a body prominence</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="method-elbow-and-knee-bandaging">METHOD: Elbow and knee bandaging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#method-elbow-and-knee-bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Let the patient sit or lie down in a comfortable position</li>
<li>Support the injured limb with the joint partially flexed if possible</li>
<li>Place the tail of the bandage on the inner side of the joint</li>
<li>Pass the bandage over and round to the outside of the joint</li>
<li>Make one and a half turns round the joint so that the end of the bandage is fixed and the joint is covered</li>
<li>Pass the bandage to the inner side of the limb just above the joint. Make a turn round the limb covering the upper half of the bandage from the first turn</li>
<li>Pass bandage from inner side of the limb to just below the joint. Make one diagonal turn below the joint to cover the lower half of the bandage from the first straight turn.</li>
<li>Continue to bandage diagonally above and below the joint in a figure of eight ensuring that the bandaged area covers two thirds of previous turn each time.</li>
<li>Secure the end of the bandage with strapping or alternatives</li>
<li>Check the circulation distal of beyond the bandage as soon as you have finished. If the bandage is too tight, unroll it and reapply it more loosely.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="triangular-bandaging">TRIANGULAR BANDAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#triangular-bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Triangular bandages are used in securing hand, foot or scalp dressing or to form slings to support an injured upper limb</p>
<p>Tying a reef knot:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Pass the left end (grey) over and under the right end (white)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lift both ends of the bandage above the rest of the material</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pass the right end (grey) over and under the left end (white)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pull ends to tighten the knot</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="untying-a-reef-knot">Untying a reef knot<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#untying-a-reef-knot" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Pull one end and one piece of bandage firmly so that it straightens</li>
<li>Hold the knot and pull the straightened end through it</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="scalp-bandaging">Scalp bandaging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#scalp-bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Let the patient sit or lie down in a comfortable position</li>
<li>Fold a hem along the base of the bandage and place the bandage on the patients head with the hem underneath and the centre of the base just above his/her eye brows. Allow the bandage to fall back over the top of the head.</li>
<li>Wrap the ends of the bandage securely around the patient's head, tucking the hem just above his/her ears</li>
<li>Cross the above two free ends over the point (tail) and tie them in a single turn (half of a knot) at the nape of the patients neck</li>
<li>Bring the free ends around to the forehead and tie a complete square knot (reel knot)</li>
<li>Truck the hanging tail over and into the half knot behind the head or secure it above the half knot with a safety pin</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hand-and-foot-bandaging">HAND AND FOOT BANDAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hand-and-foot-bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Let the patient sit or lie down in a comfortable position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Support the injured limb in the functional position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the tail of the bandage on the inner side of the wrist at the base of the thumb/ankle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Make two straight turns around the wrist/ankle</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Loop the bandage diagonally to the little finger/ little toe and make one and a half complete turns around the fingers/toes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue figure of 8 or spiral pattern leaving the patient's thumb/heel from bandage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Secure bandage at ankle/wrist with strapping or other material</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the circulation distal to the bandage</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tubular-bandaging">TUBULAR BANDAGING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tubular-bandaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Let the patient sit or lie down in a comfortable position</li>
<li>Cut a piece of tubular gauze about two and a half times the length of the injured finger/toe</li>
<li>Slide the whole length of tubular gauze onto the applicator, than gently slide the applicator over the patient's finger</li>
<li>Holding the end of the gauze on the finger, pull the applicator slightly beyond the finger top to leave a gauze layer on the finger. Twist the applicator twice to seal the bandage over the end of finger.</li>
<li>Gently push the applicator back over the finger to apply the second layer of gauze. Once all of it has been applied, remove the applicator from the finger</li>
<li>Secure the gauze at the base of the finger with adhesive tape/ strapping</li>
<li>NOTE; where tubular bandages are not available, we can use rolled gauze to do finger/toe bandaging. On the last turn around the finger, gauze is pulled over the top of the hand/ foot(dorsum) to extend over the wrist/ankle joints split into two and tied to secure the bandage</li>
<li>Check circulation distal to the bandaged area.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arm-sling-application">ARM-SLING APPLICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arm-sling-application" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>An arm sling provides support for an injured upper arm, wrist or fore arm or a single rib fracture</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Let the patient sit in the most comfortable position</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assist the injured arm across the chest with elbows flexed</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place the triangular bandage with the hemmed base parallel with the patient's body, in level with the little fingernail and the tail/point towards the elbow of injured side.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pass the upper end under the injured arm and pull it around the neck to the opposite shoulder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fold the lower end of the bandage up over the fore arm and bring it to meet the upper end at the shoulder</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tie a reef knot on the injured side at the hollow just above clavicle. Tuck both free ends of the bandage under the knot to pad it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fold the point and tuck it in behind the elbow and secure with a safety pin.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit4-first-aid-kit">UNIT4; FIRST AID KIT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit4-first-aid-kit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objective">OBJECTIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Identify and use contents in the first the first aid kit</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-aid-kits">FIRST AID KITS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-aid-kits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>First aid kits may be kept in cloth bags or plastic or metal boxes. They are often labeled with a symbol such as those on the upper right. A first aid kit may contain many items, but basic items that can help with first aid include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Gloves for the helper's hands made of vinyl, latex or nitrile to protect the helper's hands from blood</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dressings of cloth that can be put on wounds to stop bleeding, much like gauze pads or sanitary napkins</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bandages of gauze or cloth which hold dressings tightly over wounds; sometimes these are in rolls</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rolls of tape to hold on dressings and bandages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Scissors that can be used to cut tape, to open clothing and to make more bandages and dressings</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>CPR masks or barriers to make it sanitary for a helper to breathe into someone's mouth, which is one part of CPR</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blanket made of cloth or Mylar ("space blanket") to cover a sick or hurt person to keep them warm</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A small first aid book which shows how to do first aid and reminds people who have been trained</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Adhesive strips (a small piece of tape with a bit of cloth in the center), special dressings such as moleskin for blisters, and antiseptic creams for small wounds</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tweezers to remove stingers, and tongs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>first-aid manual different sizes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>adhesive tape</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>adhesive bandages in severe sizes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>elastic bandage</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>a splint</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>antiseptic wipes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>soap</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>antibiotic ointment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>antiseptic solution (like hydrogen peroxide or saline)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hydrocortisone cream (1%)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>acetaminophen and ibuprofen</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>extra prescription medications (if the family is going on vacation)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>sharp scissors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>safety pins</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>disposable instant cold packs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>calamine lotion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>thermometer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>tooth preservation kit</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>flashlight and extra batteries</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>thermal shock blanket</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>mouthpiece for administering CPR</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>blanket (stored nearby)</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-6-moving-and-handling-casualties">UNIT 6' MOVING AND HANDLING CASUALTIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-6-moving-and-handling-casualties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positioning-and-moving-the-victim">POSITIONING AND MOVING THE VICTIM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positioning-and-moving-the-victim" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This chapter outlines the techniques and procedures that underpin first aid, including moving a casualty. Usually, a first aider is not expected to move an injured person, but in some circumstances—such as when a casualty is in immediate danger—it may be necessary. The key principles for moving casualties are described here. Information is also given on making an assessment of the risks involved in moving a casualty or assisting a casualty to safety. A guide to the equipment and materials commonly found in a first aid kit is given, with information on how and when to use them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To assess the casualty's condition.</li>
<li>To comfort and reassure the casualty.</li>
<li>To maintain a casualty's privacy and dignity.</li>
<li>To use a first aid technique relevant to the injury.</li>
<li>To apply good handling techniques if moving a casualty.</li>
<li>To obtain appropriate help: call 911 for emergency help if you suspect serious injury or illness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="removing-clothing">REMOVING CLOTHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-clothing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To make a thorough examination of a casualty, obtain an accurate diagnosis, or give treatment, you may have to remove some of his clothing. This should be done with the minimum of disturbance to the casualty and with his agreement if possible. Remove as little clothing as possible and do not damage clothing unless it is necessary. If you need to cut a garment, try to cut along the seams, keeping the clothing clear of the casualty's injury. Maintain the casualty's privacy</p>
<p>and prevent exposure to cold. Stop if removing clothing increases the casualty's discomfort or pain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="removing-clothing-in-lower-body-injuries">REMOVING CLOTHING IN LOWER BODY INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-clothing-in-lower-body-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="shoes">Shoes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#shoes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Untie any laces, support the ankle, and carefully pull the shoe off by the heel. To remove long boots, you may need to cut them down the back seat.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="socks">Socks<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#socks" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Remove socks by pulling them off gently. If this is not possible, lift each sock away from the leg and cut the fabric with a pair of scissors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="trousers">Trousers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trousers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Gently pull up the pant leg to expose the calf and knee or pull down from the waist. If you need to cut clothing, lift it clear of the casualty's injury.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="removing-clothing-in-upper-body-injuries">REMOVING CLOTHING IN UPPER BODY INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-clothing-in-upper-body-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="jackets">Jackets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#jackets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Support the injured arm. Undo any fastenings on the jacket and gently pull the garment off the casualty's shoulders. Remove the arm on the uninjured side from its sleeve. Pull the garment around to the injured side of the body and ease it off the injured arm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sweaters-and-sweatshirts">Sweaters and sweatshirts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sweaters-and-sweatshirts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>With clothing that cannot be unfastened, begin by easing the arm on the uninjured side out of its sleeve. Next, roll up the garment and stretch it over the casualty's head. Finally, slip off the other sleeve of the garment, taking care not to disturb her arm on the injured side.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="removing-headgear">REMOVING HEADGEAR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-headgear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Protective headgear, such as a horseback rider's, bicyclist's, or motorcyclist's helmet, is best left on; it should be removed only if absolutely necessary, for example, if you cannot maintain an open airway. If the item does need to be removed, the casualty should do this herself if possible; otherwise, you and a helper should remove it. Support the head and neck at all times and keep the head aligned with the spine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="removing-an-open-face-or-riding-helmet">REMOVING AN OPEN-FACE OR RIDING HELMET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-an-open-face-or-riding-helmet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Undo or cut through the chinstrap. Support the casualty's head and neck, keeping them aligned with the spine. Hold the lower jaw with one hand and support the neck with the other hand.</li>
<li>Ask a helper to grip the sides of the helmet and pull them apart to take pressure off the head, then lift the helmet upward and backward.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="removing-a-full-face-helmet">REMOVING A FULL-FACE HELMET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#removing-a-full-face-helmet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Undo or cut the straps. Working from the base of the helmet, ease your fingers underneath the rim. Support the back of the neck with one hand and hold the lower jaw firmly. Ask a helper to hold the helmet with both hands.</li>
<li>Continue to support the casualty's neck and lower jaw. Ask your helper, working from above, to tilt the helmet backward (without moving the head) and gently lift the front of the helmet clear of the casualty's chin.</li>
<li>Maintain support on the head and neck. Ask your helper to tilt the helmet forward slightly so that it will pass over the base of the casualty's skull, and then to lift it straight off the casualty's head.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="casualty-handling">CASUALTY HANDLING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#casualty-handling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Caution</p>
<ol>
<li>Do not approach a casualty if doing so puts your own life in danger.</li>
<li>Do not move a casualty unless there is an emergency situation that demands you take immediate action.</li>
</ol>
<p>When giving first aid you should leave a casualty in the position in which you find him until medical help arrives. Only move him if he is in imminent danger, and even then only if it is safe for you to approach and you have the training and equipment to carry out the move. A casualty should be moved quickly if he is in imminent danger from:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drowning;</li>
<li>Fire or he is in an area that is filling with smoke;</li>
<li>Explosion or gunfire;</li>
<li>A collapsing building or other structure.</li>
</ul>
<p>ASSESSING THE RISK OF MOVING A CASUALTY</p>
<p>If it is necessary to move a casualty, consider the following before you start.</p>
<ul>
<li>Is the task necessary? Usually, the casualty can be assessed and treated in the position in which you find him.</li>
<li>What are his injuries or conditions, and will a move make them worse?</li>
<li>Can the casualty move himself? Ask the casualty if he feels able to move.</li>
<li>The weight and size of the casualty.</li>
<li>Can anyone help? If so, are you and any helpers trained and physically fit?</li>
<li>Will you need protective equipment to enter the area, and do you have it?</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Is there any equipment available to assist with moving the casualty and are you trained to use it? Is there enough space around the casualty to move him safely?
&gt; What sort of ground will you be crossing?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assisting-a-casualty-safely">ASSISTING A CASUALTY SAFELY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assisting-a-casualty-safely" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If you need to move a casualty, take the following steps to ensure safety.</p>
<ol>
