<li>Select a method relevant to the situation, the casualty's condition, and the help and equipment that is available.</li>
<li>Use a team. Appoint one person to coordinate the move and make sure that the team understands exactly what to do.</li>
<li>Plan your move carefully and make sure that everyone is prepared.</li>
<li>Prepare any equipment and make sure that the team and equipment are in position.</li>
<li>Use the correct technique to avoid injuring the casualty, yourself, or any helpers.</li>
<li>Ensure the safety and comfort of the casualty, yourself, and any helpers.</li>
<li>Always explain to the casualty what is happening, and encourage him to cooperate as much as possible.</li>
<li>Position yourself as close as possible to the casualty's body.</li>
<li>Adopt a stable base, with your feet shoulder width apart, so that you remain well balanced and maintain good posture at all times during the procedure.</li>
<li>Use the strongest muscles in your legs and arms to power the move. Bend your knees.</li>
</ol>
<p>BURNS AND SCALDS ELECTRICAL WOUNDS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burns-and-scalds">BURNS AND SCALDS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns-and-scalds" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Burns are injuries that can be caused by contact with heat, electricity, or chemicals</li>
<li>Heat burns can be caused by contact with fire, a hot surface, a hot liquid, or steam</li>
<li>If someone with a burn gets too cold, they can get hypothermia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burns-types">BURNS TYPES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns-types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Dry Burns</strong> – hot surfaces, fire, friction
<strong>Scalds</strong> – hot liquids, hot fat or oil, steam
<strong>Cold Injury</strong> – freezing temperatures, refrigerants
<strong>Radiation Burns</strong> – sunburn, ultraviolet lamps
<strong>Chemical Burns</strong> – Acids, alkalis, cleaning products
<strong>Electrical Burns</strong> – Low voltage, Lightning, High voltage</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burns-classification">BURNS CLASSIFICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; <strong>Superficial</strong> – Redness, Mild swelling, Tenderness,
&gt; <strong>Partial-Thickness</strong> – Blisters, Swelling, Weeping fluids, Pain
&gt; <strong>Full-thickness</strong> – Leathery, waxy pearly grey, charred skin</p>
<p>The severity of a burn is dependent upon five factors.</p>
<ul>
<li>Extent of the burn (surface area damage)</li>
<li>Part (s) of the hot body burnt, especially <strong>airway damage</strong></li>
<li>Depth of the burnt area.</li>
<li>Age and physical condition of casualty.</li>
<li>Associated injuries sustained (i.e. head injuries, blast, damage to lungs, fractures)</li>
</ul>
<p>General principles for managing burns</p>
<ul>
<li>Follow DRSABC</li>
<li>cool the burnt area with sterile water</li>
</ul>
<p>Cover burn either with a non-adherent burn, dressing, plastic wrap, clean dressing or loosely applied aluminum foil
Prevent infection by covering the burn wound
Minimize shock by reassurance</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-6cd1ac62.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-00962a9a.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="burns-classification">Burns classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns-classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-not-s-for-burns">Do not's for burns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-not-s-for-burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do Not: Burst blisters or touch the burnt area</li>
<li>Apply any creams or ointments</li>
<li>Remove clothing that is stuck to the skin</li>
<li>Apply adhesive dressings</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="superficial-burns-treatment">SUPERFICIAL BURNS TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#superficial-burns-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wear disposable gloves</li>
<li>Cool burn with cold water for 10 minutes</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Remove clothing or jewellery</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="partial-thickness-burns-treatment">PARTIAL-THICKNESS BURNS TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#partial-thickness-burns-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Wear disposable gloves</li>
<li>Remove clothing or jewellery</li>
<li>Cool burn with water for 10 minutes</li>
<li>Cover burn with dry, non-adhesive, sterile dressing</li>
<li>Treat for Shock</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="full-thickness-burns-treatment">FULL-THICKNESS BURNS TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#full-thickness-burns-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Call 9-9-9/112 for an ambulance</li>
<li>Wear disposable gloves</li>
<li>Remove clothing or jewellery</li>
<li>Cover burn with dry, non-stick, sterile dressing</li>
<li>Monitor airway and breathing, provide care as needed</li>
<li>Treat for shock</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemical-burns">CHEMICAL BURNS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Results from caustic or corrosive substance: Acids, Alkalis, Organic compounds</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="treatment">Treatment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Dry Chemical – Brush chemical off skin</li>
<li>Wet Chemical</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Flush skin with water for 20 minutes</li>
<li>Remove contaminated clothing and jewellery – Gloves on</li>
<li>Cover the burn with a dry, sterile or clean dressing</li>
<li>Seek medical care</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chemicals-in-the-eye-treatment">CHEMICALS IN THE EYE TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemicals-in-the-eye-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Flush with warm sterile water for 20 minutes</li>
<li>Position head appropriately</li>
<li>Loosely bandage both eye</li>
<li>Seek immediate medical care</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chemical-burns-remember">Chemical Burns REMEMBER!<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chemical-burns-remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Note the name of the substance that caused the burn</li>
<li>Wear protective rubber gloves</li>
<li>Beware of fumes</li>
<li>Irrigate for longer than you would for thermal burns</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electric-injuries">ELECTRIC INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electric-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Electricity can burn the body on the inside and outside</li>
<li>Electricity can stop breathing or cause a deadly abnormal heart rhythm</li>
<li>Electricity may leave only small marks on the body</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electrical-burns-thermal-burn-flame-arc-burn-flash-and-true-electrical-contact">ELECTRICAL BURNS: Thermal burn (flame) Arc burn (flash) and True electrical (contact)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electrical-burns-thermal-burn-flame-arc-burn-flash-and-true-electrical-contact" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="treatment">Treatment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Make the scene safe – disconnect the power at fuse box or circuit breaker</li>
<li>Check ABC and Check for spinal injuries</li>
<li>Cover burns and wounds</li>
<li>Treat for shock</li>
<li>Call 9-9-9/112 for an ambulance</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electric-shock">ELECTRIC SHOCK<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electric-shock" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Avoid direct contact with the victim</li>
<li>Before touching the victim</li>
<li>wear plastic gloves</li>
<li>stand on dry wooden chair</li>
<li>push the victim with a wooden ladder or chair or wooden stick</li>
<li>Disconnect power if possible</li>
<li>Do C.P.R. if needed</li>
<li>Treat burns</li>
<li>Call for Medical Help</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-4253912c.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>

Manager QHSE</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cadiopulmonarly-resustation">CADIOPULMONARLY RESUSTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cadiopulmonarly-resustation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Another set of goals for keeping a badly hurt person alive is sometimes called "C-A-B" -DRCAB
&gt; 'keep <strong>blood inside</strong> the body and the <strong>heart beating</strong>'</p>
<p>CPR is as easy as
C-A-B</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-eb14d8f8.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg">
Compressions Push hard and fast on the center of the victim's chest</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-91032fc6.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg">
Airway Tilt the victim's head back and lift the chin to open the airway</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-ae642d7f.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg">
Breathing Give mouth-to-mouth rescue breaths</p>
<p>American Heart Association</p>

<p>Learn and Live</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-someone-is-unconscious-and-breathing">. IF SOMEONE IS UNCONSCIOUS AND BREATHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-someone-is-unconscious-and-breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If a person is unconscious but is breathing and has no other life-threatening conditions, they should be placed in the recovery position until help arrives</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-someone-is-unconscious-and-not-breathing">IF SOMEONE IS UNCONSCIOUS AND NOT BREATHING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-someone-is-unconscious-and-not-breathing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If a person is not breathing normally after an incident, call for an ambulance and start CPR straight away. Mouth to Mouth respiration rate at 16/min</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-d4725fed.jpeg" alt="img-32.jpeg"></p>
<p>A "cardiac arrest" is when your heart stops beating. This is not the same as a "heart attack", although a heart attack may lead to a cardiac arrest. There are numerous causes of cardiac arrests, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>A disturbance in the heart rhythm</li>
<li>Drugs/poisoning</li>
<li>Heart disease / a heart attack</li>
<li>Traumatic injury/blood loss</li>
<li>Anaphylaxis</li>
</ul>
<p>If a cardiac arrest occurs, blood will stop circulating around the body. Breathing will also cease as well though it may not stop completely for several minutes.</p>
<p>Without a supply of oxygen, brain cells in the start to die in about 3 – 5 minutes leading to brain damage and death.</p>
<p>The purpose of CPR is to keep oxygenated blood flowing around the body to keep the vital organs alive. CPR itself will not restart someone's heart; it just keeps them alive until a defibrillator arrives. A defibrillator is a device which delivers an electrical shock to the heart to restart it.</p>
<p>How help someone who has collapsed</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-770b91f8.jpeg" alt="img-33.jpeg"></p>
<p>DRS ABC to remember what to do:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Danger: Check for any dangers to yourself. Response: Check for a response from the casualty.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Airway: open their airway</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Breathing: Check for normal breathing (regular breaths) for up to 10 seconds
Compressions: If the casualty is not breathing, you should call an ambulance and start chest compressions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once you've found someone isn't breathing, and there is no circulation you should start CPR straight by administering 30 chest compressions...</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Send for AED. (Automated external defibrillator): An AED is reliable, safe, computerized device that delivers electric shocks to a casualty in cardiac arrest when the ECG rhythm is one that is likely to respond to a shock. Simplicity of operation is a key feature: controls are kept to a minimum, ‘voice and visual prompts’ guide rescuers.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>After 30 chest compressions, you should give 2 rescue breaths. You should aim for a rate of 100 – 120 chest compressions a minute.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-b1fe4386.jpeg" alt="img-34.jpeg"></p>
<p>In order for the heart to be restarted, it may require an electrical shock from a defibrillator or drugs given by a paramedic/doctor. However, good quality chest compressions will significantly increase the chance of the defibrillator being able to restart the heart.</p>
<p>You should only stop doing CPR if:</p>
<ul>
<li>A defibrillator arrives and is about to be used</li>
<li>The casualty shows signs of life: coughing, breathing etc.</li>
<li>You are asked to stop by a healthcare professional (ambulance crew etc.)</li>
</ul>
<p>Ideally, you should only carry out CPR for a couple of minutes before swapping with someone else. This is to ensure that the chest compressions remain of good quality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>INFANT CPR—rescue breathing'</p>
<ul>
<li>: use 2 fingers for; 30 compressions</li>
<li>PUBERTY CHILD</li>
<li>rescue breathing'</li>
<li>30 compressions; use one palm hand heel</li>
<li>2 rescue breaths</li>
<li>30;2</li>
<li>remember pocket breathing mask/face shield for protection</li>
<li>never use AED on infants under one year</li>
</ul>
<p>For Cardiac arrest use DRCAB procedure. This is because the heart has stopped and there is no circulation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="poisoning">POISONING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="poisoning">Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Poisoning is any substance that causes injury, illness or death when introduced into the body. There are different types of poisoning:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ingested poisons are introduced through the mouth by eating or drinking poisonous substances.</li>
<li>Inhaled poisons are introduced through the lungs by inhaling industrial gases, fumes from fire, chemical vapors and petrol and engine exhaust.</li>
<li>Absorbed poisons are absorbed through the skin via contact with poisonous sprays such as pesticides and insecticides.</li>
</ul>
<p>Do's:</p>
<ul>
<li>Check the danger, response, airway, breathing and the blood circulation of the victim</li>
<li>Give milk or water to dilute down the poison</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs and prevent shock</li>
<li>Observe the amount and color of vomitus</li>
<li>Check for foreign matter in his or her mouth and remove it so that he/she can breath freely</li>
<li>Place the patient in the recovery position and wait for medical assistance.</li>
<li>Send to hospital</li>
</ul>
<p>Don'ts:</p>
<ul>
<li>Don’t induce vomiting.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dog-bites">Dog Bites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dog-bites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The aim of First Aid in case of dog bite is to prevent rabies, to reduce the risk of infection and to get medical aid as soon as possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-s">Do's :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-s" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Wipe the saliva away from the wound using a clean cloth or handkerchief.</li>
<li>Do not come in contact with the saliva that gets wiped away.</li>
<li>Wash the wound thoroughly with plenty of soap and water.</li>
<li>Cover the wound with a dry, sterile dressing.</li>
<li>Get medical aid or send the patient to the hospital as soon as possible.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="snake-bite">SNAKE BITE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#snake-bite" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-1">STEP 1<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-1" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lay the victim down and provide reassurance. CALL HELPLINE. Do not move the victim unless further danger is present.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-c7039bdc.jpeg" alt="img-35.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-2">STEP 2<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-2" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>With a broad (minimum 7.5cm wide) elastic bandage such as setopress, start at the toes (or hand if bitten on the arm) and wrap the bandage very firmly up the entire limb. If the bandage does not cover the entire limb, start with a new bandage at the point the last bandaged finished until the entire limb is covered. The compression bandage should be firm enough to reduce lymphatic movement but not constrict blood flow. Ensure you leave the tips of the toes/fingers out to monitor circulation.</p>
<p>The compression bandage should be firm enough to reduce lymphatic movement but not constrict blood flow. Ensure you leave the tips of the toes/fingers out to monitor circulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="step-3">STEP 3<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#step-3" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the entire limb has been covered, mark the bite site with a pen or some dirt from the ground. This is helpful for emergency services personnel.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-e27b4b8f.jpeg" alt="img-36.jpeg"></p>
<ol>
<li>STEP 4</li>
<li>Splint the limb (including joints) to prevent movement. For bites to the leg, this can be achieved by strapping the legs together using slings or other suitable material.</li>
<li>Bites to the arm can be supported in a sling or splinted. Do not remove the bandage once applied.</li>
<li>Make the victim comfortable and continue to provide reassurance until the arrival of emergency services.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260115-7b8a3791.jpeg" alt="img-37.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>DO NOTS</li>
<li>DO NOT wash the bite site</li>
<li>DO NOT attempt to cut the venom out of the limb</li>
<li>DO NOT attempt to suck the venom out of the limb</li>
<li>DO NOT apply a tourniquet to the limb</li>
<li>DO NOT move the person unless in immediate danger</li>
</ul>
